                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">عَذِرَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عُذْرٌ</foreign> (S, O, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">عُذُرٌ</foreign> (S, O, K) and <foreign lang="ar">عُذْرَى</foreign> (O, K) and <foreign lang="ar">مَعْذِرَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَعْذُرَةٌ</foreign> (K) [all of which are also used as simple substs.]; and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28428-1" target="اعذرهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (S, O, Msb, K;) <hi rend="ital">He excused him; freed, cleared,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">exempted, him from blame; exculpated him:</hi> (Msb:) or <hi rend="ital">he accepted his excuse:</hi> properly, <foreign lang="ar">عَذَرْتُ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">I cancelled evil conduct.</hi> (TA.) [See also <foreign lang="ar">عُذْرٌ</foreign> below.] You say, <foreign lang="ar">عَذَرْتُهُ فِيمَا صَنَعَ</foreign> (S, O, Msb) <hi rend="ital">I excused,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">exculpated, him for what he did.</hi> (Msb.) And in a trad. of El-Mikdád it is said, <foreign lang="ar">لَقَدْ <ref cref="n28428-2" target="أَعْذَرَ" n="2" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>ٱللّٰهُ إِلَيْكَ</foreign> i.e. <hi rend="ital">Verily God hath excused thee,</hi> and exempted thee from the obligation to fight against the unbelievers; for he had become extremely fat, and unable to fight. (TA.) And you say [also], <foreign lang="ar">عَذَرَهُ عَنِ الشَّىْءِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He excused him for,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">from, the thing.</hi> (MA.) [And accord. to Golius,<foreign lang="ar">عَذَرَهُ عَلَى الشَّىْءِ</foreign>, as well as <foreign lang="ar">فِى الشَّىْءِ</foreign>: but he has not mentioned his authority: see an explanation of <foreign lang="ar">عَذِيرٌ</foreign>, from which the former phrase was perhaps derived by him.] And <foreign lang="ar">عَذَرْتُهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ فُلَانٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I excused him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">held him excusable, for his conduct to such a one</hi>]; meaning, I did not blame him, but I blamed such a one. (S, * TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ يَعْذِرُنِى مِنْهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Who will excuse me,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">make my excuse, if I requite him</hi> (Msb, TA) <hi rend="ital">for his action,</hi> (Msb,) or <hi rend="ital">for his evil action,</hi> (TA,) <hi rend="ital">and will not blame me</hi> (Msb, TA) <hi rend="ital">for it?</hi> (Msb:) or <hi rend="ital">who will excuse me with respect to his case, and will not blame me for it?</hi> (Msb.) [And a similar ex. is mentioned in the TA with <foreign lang="ar">فِى</foreign> in the place of <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">عَذَرَ</foreign>, (Az, S, IKtt, O, Msb, K,) aor.

                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">عَذِرَ</orth>
                  </form>; (O, TA;) and

[<hi rend="ital">Men will not perish,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">die,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">until they are guilty of many crimes,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sins,</hi> &amp;c.; (S, O, Msb, K;) meaning, (accord. to A 'Obeyd, S, O,) <hi rend="ital">until they deserve punishment, so as to render excusable him who punishes them.</hi> (S, A, O, TA.) The Prophet said thus with respect to 'Abd-Allah Ibn-Ubeí, demanding of the people that they should excuse him for laying violent hands upon him. (TA.) [It is a phrase by which one asks for permission to retaliate, or punish, &amp;c.] And one says also, <foreign lang="ar">عَذِيرَكَ مِنْ فُلَانٍ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Bring him who will excuse thee</hi> [<hi rend="ital">for what thou hast done,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">doest,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">wilt do, to such a one</hi>]; (S, O, TA;) i. e. <hi rend="ital">bring him who will blame him and will not blame thee.</hi> (S, O.) And <foreign lang="ar">عَذيرَكَ إِيَّاىَ مِنْهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Bring thine excuse of me</hi> [<hi rend="ital">for what I have done,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">to him</hi>]. (TA.) A poet (Dhu-l-Isba' El-'Adwánee, O, TA) says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">عَذِيرَ الحَىِّ مِنْ عَدْوَا</foreign>

                     </L>

                     </L> 
                  </quote> (S, * O, * L, TA) [Bring <hi rend="ital">an excuse for the tribe, for what they have done to 'Adwán,</hi> i. e., one to another; for the tribe of 'Adwán were rent by intestine wars, in which Dhu-l-Isba' took a prominent part; (see the Essai sur l' Histoire des Arabes by Caussin de Perceval, vol. ii. p. 262;) therefore we may render the phrase, bring <hi rend="ital">an excuse for the tribe, 'Adwán,</hi> regarding <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ</foreign> as redundant in this instance, like as it is in <foreign lang="ar">فَٱجْتَنِبُوا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱلرِّجْسَ مِنَ ٱلْأَوْثَانِ</foreign>, in the Kur xxii. 31; and then proceed thus: <hi rend="ital">they were the serpent of the earth</hi> (meaning <hi rend="ital">cunning, guileful, malignant,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mischievous, and strong, not neglecting to take blood-revenge,</hi> as expl. in art. <foreign lang="ar">حى</foreign> in the TA): but <hi rend="ital">some acted wrongfully against some, and were not regardful</hi> of the rights <hi rend="ital">of some: so they became subjects of talk</hi> uttered <hi rend="ital">by the raising of speech and the lowering</hi> thereof]: he means, bring an excuse for what some of them have done to some by mutual hatred and slaughter, some of them being not regardful of some; after their having been the serpent of the earth, which every one fears. (L, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">A state,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">condition,</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">حال</foreign>,) <hi rend="ital">which one desires,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">seeks after, for which,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">on account of which, he is to be excused</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">يُعْذَرُ</foreign>
